### Appreciation of protection through danger

That concludes our study of these 2 surahs. Now the question is . how is the Istiaaza and these 2 surahs even related to Surah AlFateha? Why are we studying the Istiaaza instead of studying the Fateha?

Imagine there is a huge storm coming. where would you prefer to be when the storm hits your town? Probably in your house? Your house is a symbol of safety against the storm. But the reason you appreciate that safety.  is because you understand the dangers of the storm.  yes? You cannot appreciate safety. until you understand the danger that you are being protected from. You appreciate the air conditioning in your house. because you've experienced the heat outside. You appreciate the heating in your house. because you've experienced the freezing cold outside. We human beings. we understand things through contrast. The one who truly appeciates and values food. is the one who has a true understanding of hunger. someone who has truly experienced hunger. You know. you can tell. just by looking at someone who wastes food. that this person has never experienced hunger. I'm not talking about the hunger after a tennis match when you come home and the fridge is loaded. I'm not talking about that hunger. I'm talking about the hunger in which you haven't eaten for days.  and there's nothing in the fridge at home. That man. when he gets food. you can see him appreciating the value of that food.

So Surah AlFateha is a fortress. It is a safe haven. But in order to truly appreciate its value. To truly appreciate what it has to offer us in terms of security. what must we first understand? The dangers. We needed to first understand the dangers. the evils that surround this fortress.

The Istiaaza. is the door of that fortress. that keeps the evils out.  and keeps us safe within the fortress.  So we started with the Istiaaza. we started with the dangers of evil. so that we can truly appreciate the comforts within the Fateha. That is why we started with the Istiaaza. and this is what Allah commanded us to do.

⟪ar-quote:فأذا قرأت القرآن فستعذ باللہ من الشیطان الرجیم⟫

Before you enter the fortress of Quran. seek protection . close the door on Shaytan AlRajeem. But first. understand what the Quran is protecting you from. so that you can truly appreciate its protection.

But then I started with these two surahs. Surah Naas and Surah Falaq. because they are deeply connected with surah AlFateha.  I want to quickly go over some of these connections InshaAllah!

The first connection is the cyclic pattern in the recitation of Quran. When we recite the Quran what surah do we begin with? We begin with the Fateha. And before we begin fateha. what do we recite? The Istiaaza. We say  ⟪ar:اعوذ باللہ من الشیطان الرجیم⟫ .

So we begin with the Istiaaza. then we start Surah AlFateha. which is the essence of the entire Quran. and then we continue reciting the surahs. until we complete the recitation of Quran. But at the end of our recitation. what are the last 2 surahs we encounter? Surah Falaq and Surah Naas. both surahs of the Istiaaza. We start with the Istiaaza and we end with the Istiaaza.

So think of the Quran as a beautiful and comfortable house. a safe haven. Your fortress of solitude.  Before you enter it. you seek protection from evil.  and then you enter the house. Why? so that you can enjoy all the comforts the house has to offer. that is the recitation of the Quran. And then when you're ready to step outside. you again go through the Istiaaza in the form of Surah Falaq and Naas. so that you remain protected while you're outside the house.  So it protects us on both ends. when we enter the fortress of Quran. and when we exit it.

But then once you complete the recitation of the Quran. immediately after that what do you do? You read a dua (the dua recited at the completion of Quran) and then you recite what surah again? Surah AlFateha. You started quran with the Istiaaza. you ended it with the istiaaza. and the end of it you recite the Fateha again. And then you start the entire process again.

When you step out of your house. you go to school or work. where do you end up returning in the evening? Back to your home again. So there is this cyclic pattern in the recitation of Quran with protection on both ends.

There is something really important to understand about this analogy between a house and the Quran. As I said. we always begin our day by leaving our homes.  and at the end of our day. we return back to our homes. But where do we spend our entire day? Outside the house. At school or at work. at tennis or basketball. at tutions. at whatever. We spend most of our time outside the house. Yes?  So home is not a place we spend most of our time. We spend it ouside. But home is a place. where we gather our energies. we eat and drink and relax and sleep. those are all actions that replenish our energy. recharge our battery. correct? These things refresh us. they revitalize us. But where do we actually spend this energy? Outside our homes. Is that clear?

A true believer has the same relationship with the Quran. He enters the fortress of quran. to replenish his energies. to revitalize himself with the teachings of Quran. But where is he going to actually execute those teachings? In the ouside world. in duniya. So the idea is that we as momins. as believers. we keep coming back to the Quran constantly. to remind ourselves of its teachings. and then go back into the world.  to act upon what we have learnt.

But as soon as we step outside. who do we encounter? Our greatest enemy. Who has openely declared his animosity agianst us. We encounter Iblees or one of his shaytans. who openly declared to Allah.

⟪ar-quote:قَالَ فَبِمَآ أَغْوَيْتَنِى لَأَقْعُدَنَّ لَهُمْ صِرَطَكَ ٱلْمُسْتَقِيمَ⟫

because you were the one who expelled me from jannah. I will sit waiting for them . to ambush them on your straight path. ⟪ar:صِرَطَكَ ٱلْمُسْتَقِيمَ⟫ . Which surah mentions the straight path?

⟪ar:اھدنا الصراط المستقیم⟫.  Surah Fateha mentions the straight path.

We are asking allah to protect us from iblees because he is on a mission to get us off the straight path. We learn the details of how to walk on the straight path in the Quran. but when we step outside and try walking on that straight path. who do we find sitting there. waiting to ambush us? Iblees. And that's why these two surahs of protection. falaq and naas. are so intimately connected with Surah AlFateha. Because we need Allahs protection when we are walking that straight path. because we know that Iblees is going to be there. trying to get us off.

Then from a thematic stand point. the themes of these 2 surahs.  Falaq and Naas. they have a powerful connections with AlFateha. Surah Fatiha is about the ⟪ar:استعانۃ⟫. We'll study this term later. But ⟪ar:استعانۃ⟫means seeking help. Which is what Surah AlFateha is all about.  . ⟪ar:ایاک نعبد و ایاک نستعین⟫. It is you we worship and it is you we turn to for help. So in Fateha. we have two statements for the Istiaana. ⟪ar:ایاک نعبد⟫ and ⟪ar:ایاک نستعین⟫.  and here we have two surahs for the Istiaaza. for protection.  Surah Falaq and Surah Naas. There we ask Allah for help.  here we ask Allah for protection. You've heard of positve and negative reinformcements, right? In Fateha we ask Allah. for help in accomplishign a task. in ⟪ar:معوذِتین⟫we ask Allah for His protection against elements.  that are trying to keep us from completing that task.

Then the words of these surahs. especially Surah Naas. they complement the words of AlFateha.

In Surah Naas we seek protection of the owner and master of all people. ⟪ar:رب الناس⟫ .  in AlFateha. what do we call him? ⟪ar:رب العلمین⟫ . owner and master of all worlds.

In fateha we say ⟪ar:مالک یوم الدین⟫ . In Surah AlNaas we say ⟪ar:ملک الناس⟫ . both Maalik and Malik. they both have the same root word

In fateha we say ⟪ar:ایاک نعبد⟫ . It is you we worship.  and who is worship done for? A diety? An Ilah? Right? So in Surah AlNaas we say ⟪ar:الہ الناس .⟫

Then we see that the ⟪ar:معوذِتین⟫. they are the two surahs of protection. and in Surah AlFateh was ask Allah to keep us away from 2 kinds of people.  or two bad influences. ⟪ar:مغضوب علیھم ولا الضالین .⟫

And then in Surah Fateha. just as we have these two negative influences. the ⟪ar:مغضوب علیھم ولا الضالین⟫ . In Surah Naas. we have two categories of evil that we seek protection from  ⟪ar:من الجنۃ و الناس⟫. from the jin and people. SubhanAllah!  There are these incredible connections between these 2 surahs and Surah AlFateha. The way in which quran begins. perfectly complements the way in which it ends.

Then another remarkable thing is the parallel between the singular and plural forms used between the two surahs.  The very word used in the ⟪ar:معوذتین⟫for seeking protection.  is in the singular form. ⟪ar:اعوذ⟫. but the words used in the Fateha for seeking guidance. are all in plural. we say ⟪ar:ایاک نعبد⟫  not⟪ar:ایاک أعبدُ⟫ .  So there is this balance betwen sigular and plural. because the things we ask for in the Fateha. we need them as a group. as a group of muslims. or a group of momins. or a group of sulemanis. Look at it however you will. but fateha has a group theme going on. because our communication with Allah in Fateha.  is as a group. Not as individuals. We speak to him. seeking his guidance. collectively.

But when it comes to the waswas of the shytan.  is it a collective thing or is it an individual thing? It's an individual thing. Therefore in the ⟪ar:معوذِتین⟫ . the theme is indvidual not collective. because these 2 surahs ask for allahs protection on a very personal and indvidual level. and therefore the verb usage is singular too. 

I misjudged the level of my audience.

These sessions are not for kids

<!-- section 8 (id=5714, raw_sort=8): Allah created me from fire and him from clay -->
We took a very detailed look at the various pieces and components of the Istiaaza. We studied Surah AlFalaq and AlNaas. We learnt things about the protector. the kind of protection He offers. and the nature of the enemy we are seeking protection from. We also learnt the requirements of seeking that protection.  Now to conclude. I want to tie all these pieces together. We saw the parts. now let's look at how these parts come together to form a complete whole.

Iblees rebellion

So what I want to talk about today. and in the next couple of sessions. is about this passage from Surah Aale Imran. which talks about the creation of Adam AS and the disobedience and rebellion of Iblees. This passage talks about when it all began. If we truly understand the purpose and the teachings of this passage. it will answer most. if not all of our questions about what Shaytan is trying to do. What his end game is. And what are the things we need to be aware of.

I think I've said this before. but I'll say it again. that the purpose of Quranic stories. is never the story itself. We listen to these bedtime stories like Aladdin. and Cinderella. and all these Once upon a time tales. And then we listen to these Quranic stories.  and sometimes we start thinking of them in the same way. Just like Cinderella is a nice bed time story for children. the story of Adam and Hawwa also becomes a nice story in our minds.  So the first thing is that we need to change our perceptions about these stories. And the first step towards that goal.  is to understand that the purpose of these Quranic stories . is NEVER the story itself. Using these stories. Allah is always trying to explain a principle from His rule book. He is trying to explain a divine law. He's giving us a clear warning and news of how things work in his divine system. There is a system or framework within which we humans operate. and then there is a framework within which Allah operates. And Quran is our window into that divine setup.

So the idea behind these quranic stories is. Allah saying.  Look! This is what happened to the people who came before you. This is how they were confronted with evil. This is how they battled it. or this is how they succumbed to it. This is what they used to say. This is how they used to think. So look where they ended up!.  Learn from it. Don't repeat the same mistakes they made. otherwise what happend to them.  is going to happen to you too. And also study the lives of those who succeeded before you. Because if you make the same smart choices that led them to success. you too will become successful.

That is the purpose of these Quranic stories. to give us working examples and set precedents for us. because as they say. History repeats itself.

And Rasul Allah stated this in a Hadees.

⟪ar-quote:لَتَتَّبِعُنَّ سَنَنَ مَنْ قَبْلَكُمْ شِبْرًا بِشِبْرٍ، وَذِرَاعًا بِذِرَاعٍ، حَتَّى لَوْ سَلَكُوا جُحْرَ ضَبٍّ لَسَلَكْتُمُوهُ⟫

You shall follow the footsteps of those before you, inch by inch and mile by mile, to the degree that if they entered the hole of a lizard.  you will follow them too

Today we are all faced with the exact same challenges. that were faced by prophets and people of their times before us. It's form may be different. it's exterior may be different. even it's intensity may be different. but the principles are still the same. It's still based on the same root evils. greed, arrogance, jealousy, passions, desires. Nothing has changed.  And the Quran presents the solution to all those problems.

So if we truly want to understand the workings and the true mechanations of Shaytan. the only way to do that. is an in-depth study of the story of Adam AS and Iblees . Because this story of Adam AS is in fact our story. The challenges of Adam AS are in fact our challenges. He is the original template.  What happend to him. is what's happening to us.

---

Story of Adam Iblees

So the story of Adam AS and Iblees. is the story of humility and arrogance.  And this story has three parts. The first part is the creation of Adam and the rebellion of Ibless. We'll look at that first. The second part is the humiliation and revenge of Iblees against Adam AS.  in getting him and his wife Hawwa. cast out of Jannah. And the third part is the response of Adam and Hawwa AS. versues the reaction of Iblees once they get cast out of Jannah.

So let's begin with the first part.  Talking about the creation of Adam AS. Allah says in the Quran.
⟪ar-quote:وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَكُمْ ثُمَّ صَوَّرْنَكُمْ⟫

We created you. we moulded you. In other words Allah says.  I know who you are. what you like.  because I made you. I know how I fashioned you.  I know the things I put inside you. I know every one of your body parts.  and I know every single temptations and craving that you have. and then He says.
⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ ٱسْجُدُوا۟ لِآدَمَ⟫

and then I asked all the angles to make sajda to you. I honored you above angels. I created in you the potential that could elevate you above angels.

### Linguistic meaning of SAJDAH

Let's understand this word Sajda. It's a beautiful word. The ancient Arabs used the word Sajada. for a camel when it would lower itself before the rider. so that he could mount it. It was used in that sense. ⟪ar:سجد الأبل⟫ they would say. when the camel would lower itself. and submit its will. to the will of its rider. Meaning the camel would allow its rider to steer it in whatever direction he wants.

So that's what sajda means in the truest sense of the word. To pay respect. or honor. by lowering oneself before a greater being. Just as the camel honors and glorifies its rider. by submitting before him. And that takes extreme humility. Because if you compare a camel to a human being. from a physical stand point. there truly is no comparison. A camel is massive compared to a human being. The strength of a camel is enormous compared to that of a human being. A camel can go for days in the extreme heat of the desert without water. a human would die of thirst. A camel can lift loads.  that would be way beyond the capacity of even the strongest human being. And yet this extremely powerful. extremely capable. this mighty creature lowers itself before a human being. It submits its will to a human being because it understands that it cannot find its path without its master.

When we fall in Sajda before Allah. it is a gesture of surrendering ourselves. surrendering our will. become humble before the will of our master. Because like the camel we too sometimes think we are superior. Our ego is our camel.  Why do I need Allah in my life? . I have money. I have power. I have status. Why do I need to submit to anyone? I am in control of my life. A camel could have the same attitude towards man. but then it would die of thirst wouldn't it? Because no matter how powerful and capable the camel thinks it is. it still needs a human being to guide it to water in a desert. That's why the camel submits itself to its owner. That's the camel's sajda.

Similarly my true sajda to Allah would be to submit the reins of my life. my will . my decisions. in the hands of my master. Letting not MY will. but the will of my master steer me through life. To let him walk me through beautiful pastures of ease.  if He so desires. and to walk me through the dry barren scorching lands of trials and hardships. if He so desires. That is the true meaning of the word Sajda. To give up oneself. to surrender one's will to the will of our master. like the camel gives itself up in the hands of its rider. like the ship that gives itself up in the hands of the wind.  ⟪ar:السَّفِینَۃُ تَسجُدُ لِلرِّیحِ⟫ . the arabs would say.

Another beautiful meaning of the words sajda. is to bend and lower oneself.  because of the weight of the bounties that are placed upon it. For example the Arabs would say ⟪ar:سَجَدَتْ النَّخْلَۃ⟫. The palm tree bent down.  by the abundance of its fruit. The weight of Allah's blessings in our lives should force us fall in sajda before Him. 

So this is what sajda is. and especially during Salaah. Look. Putting our forehead on the ground is just a symbol. The true Sajda is that of the heart. It's not a Sajda.  if after my salaah ends. I am still going to do what I want.

And BTW. even if you think about this physically act of Sajda. what are we doing? we place our forehead on the ground. Head being the most superior part of the body. because it contains the intellect. through which we plan and design and scheme. We place that intellect on the earth. on dirt.  that lies beneath our feet. It is a symbol for surrendering our thoughts. our knowledge of what WE think is best. our plans. our schemes. before our master. It's a symbol of testifying that Ya Allah. even though you have blessed me with this amazing intellect. the greatest gift of all. MY plan. MY desires. My thoughts are nothing more than dirt before you will. That is the true level of obedience that is encapsulated in this symbolic act of Sajda. And therefore the PERFECT symbol of obedience. the PERFECT representation of obedience to Allah. is Sajdah.

---

So Allah commanded the angels to prostrate before Adam. to honor him. to resepect him. first and foremost in compliance with Allah's command. because Allah commanded them to honor him. But then also as an acknowledgment that Adam had knowledge of that which they did not.

⟪ar:وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ ٱلْأَسْمَآءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى ٱلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنۢبِـُٔونِى بِأَسْمَآءِ هَٓؤُلَآءِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَدِقِينَ⟫

Allah taught Adad all the names. then presented him before teh angels. and asked the angels. Tell me all the names if you are truthful in your claims.  First Allah established the superiority of Adam AS over angels. by his knowledge that they didn't have. THEN he asked the angels to prostrate to him. So the sajda of the angels were for two reasons. First in obedience of Allahs command. and second in the recognition of Adams superiority in knowledge over them.

⟪ar-quote:فَسَجَدُوٓا۟⟫

They all fell in sajda.

⟪ar-quote:إِلَّآ إِبْلِيسَ⟫

with the exception of iblees.

⟪ar-quote:لَمْ يَكُن مِّنَ ٱلسَّجِدِينَ⟫

He wasn't going to be from among those who would prostrate. 

Instead of saying ⟪ar:ما سجدَہُ⟫ . He did not comply.  Allah says.  ⟪ar:لَمْ يَكُن مِّنَ ٱلسَّجِدِينَ⟫. he was NEVER EVER going to be from among those who would do sajda.SubhanAllah. Allah knew all along he was not going to do it.  Allah knew his intentions all along. And it's very interesting why Allah still commanded Iblees to prostrate. knowing well that he would disobey. But I'll address that a bit later.  So Allah asks Iblees.

⟪ar-quote:قَالَ مَا مَنَعَكَ أَلَّا تَسْجُدَ إِذْ أَمَرْتُكَ⟫

Allah said. what possibly prevented you from doing sajda when I told you? When I commanded you! Why didn't you obey?

Notice here. Allah did not say why did you not do sajda when you clearly saw that Adam is more knowledgable than you!. Why didn't you comply with my command when it made sense to you.  Look what Allah says. This is the part you and I need to pay very close attention to .  ⟪ar:قَالَ مَا مَنَعَكَ أَلَّا تَسْجُدَ إِذْ أَمَرْتُكَ⟫. What did you now prostrate when I COMMANDED you to?

Sajda.  has to be done in obedience to the command. You know we sometimes think. I'll do namaaz when I understand it's important. when I understand it's purpose. In other words when I have more KNOWLEDGE about it. right? That's not what Allah questions Iblees about. He gives preference to his command OVER everything else. There is nothing wrong about learning why we should pray. In fact we MUST learn that. But the REASON for Sajda. the ONLY reason for Sajda. has to be because Allah commanded us to do so. Obedience is the FIRST and foremost reason for Sajda. Why? Because the word sajda in and of itself means. that we have already accepted Allah as our master. We have lowered ourselves before Allah so that his commands can ride us. so that his command can steer us in whatever direction He pleases.

And that's why when someone asked Imam Jaffar AsSaadiq AS. یا امام ! ھل الدین ؟؟ . Oh Imam! What is religion? He replied. الا الطاعۃ . nothing except obedience. The guidance of a camel begins when does sajda before its rider. Our guidance begins when we do Sajda before Allah.

---

Fire vs Clay

So Allah asks Iblees. What possibly prevented you from obeying. when I commanded you? Now listen to what he says. And this is the real topic of today's conversation. Everything else sorta just hinges off of it. Iblees says.

⟪ar-quote:أَنَا۠ خَيْرٌۭ مِّنْهُ⟫⟪ar-quote:. خَلَقْتَنِى مِن نَّارٍۢ وَخَلَقْتَهُۥ مِن طِينٍۢ⟫

Iblees finally gives voice to his arrogance and says.I am better than him. You created me from fire and you created him from clay.

Now within this one statement. lies the root cause of disobedience. From a linguistic statement. what Iblees said. is what's called a statement of arrogance.

⟪ar:بیان الاستکبار⟫.  The tone of this statement clearly suggests that Iblees had made up his mind. Had he not used this tone. this statement could have been open for debate. It could have been argued that maybe Iblees didn't understand. maybe he had doubts and he was trying to clear it up with Allah. But this is not what his tone suggests. Look at his words within the context. Who is he speaking to? He is speaking to Allah. He is speaking to the king of kings. He is speaking to his creator. And he says. I am better than him. It's a very definitive statement. It's a very obstinate statement. There is no room for argument or discussion in his statement. In other words. there is ABSOLUTELY no humility in his tone. It has a.  THIS IS HOW IT IS. AND THIS IS HOW ITS GONNA BE. kinda ring to it.

There's nothing wrong about asking questions if we don't understand. There's ABSOLUTELY nothing wrong with questioning things. Trying to seek answers. But the thing to keep in mind.  is to never let go of humility in that line of questioning. Because the way in which a question is presented. reveals everything about the underlying emotion. You can tell immediately if the person is filled with arrogance or if there's humility in that person.

And humility in a question means. considering other possible options. That maybe it is I who doesn't understand. Maybe I am missing something.  That MAYBE this person knows something I don't. Maybe I can learn something from his experience. Just MAYBE my parents actually might know what they're talking about. Arrogance on the other hand is. This is how I see things. this is what I believe. here are the facts. and I don't care what you think. I'm not even going to try to understand what you have to say. because you obviously don't know what you're talking about. It's my way or the highway.

That's the tone Iblees uses. I am better than him! period! You created me from fire. and you created him from clay. fire is better than clay. These are just facts. It's just simple observation. It's basic science! Therefore Allah. I don't know what you were thinking when you asked me to bow down to him. I don't think you know what you're doing. You clearly don't understand the difference between fire and clay. You're asking me to bow down to him??? Are you serious?

All of this arrogance is voiced in this one statement . ⟪ar:أَنَا۠ خَيْرٌۭ مِّنْهُ⟫

Not it all kinda seems ridiculous doesn't it. when we look at it from outside. What a horrible thing to do! Bad Iblees. Bad Iblees. right?  But now put your parents commands and wishes in the position of Allah. Because Allah is Rabb. but so are your parents.  Allah is rabb. but so are our deeni elders. We just studied that in Surah Naas. This passage is about the relationship of a creation with his Rabb. Because what did Shaytan say? ⟪ar:خَلَقْتَنِى⟫. You created me. And creator means owner. and the Arabic word for that is Rabb. Allah granted his Rububiyah. to parents over children. Allah granted his rububiyah to teachers over students. When you a child talk back to your parents with arrogance. you put yourself in the same position as Iblees.

Look. there's nothing wrong with having a dialog with your parents if you disagree. that's fine. But arrogance is what's unacceptable. It's OK if you can't see eye to eye with your parents. but it's not OK to think you are better than them. you understand more than them. You don't! You can't! You guys are kids. Most of you haven't even stepped into the real world yet. They have! So they might actually know what they're talking about. Have some trust in them.  Because this ayah is teaching us the importance of humility.  when it comes to dealing with our Rabb. Parents are the closest Rabb. You can't be humble to them. how do you expect to be humble before Allah?

Another very important lesson it teaches us . is that disobedience is not the real problem. It's what leads to disobedience that is the problem. If you notice. the corruption in Iblees took place first in his soul. His statement has two parts. Look at the first part. ⟪ar:أَنَا۠ خَيْرٌۭ مِّنْهُ⟫. I am better than him. That is the corruption of his soul. That's the arrogance in his soul. And then inevitable what follows is a justification for his disobedience. ⟪ar:خَلَقْتَنِى مِن نَّارٍۢ وَخَلَقْتَهُۥ مِن طِينٍۢ⟫. You created me from fire and you created him from clay. So what he did was. he justified his arrogance with what he thought were logical facts. with no room for any sort of dialog.

And It's not like Allah was closed to a dialog. because we just saw Allah asked him.

⟪ar-quote:قَالَ مَا مَنَعَكَ أَلَّا تَسْجُدَ إِذْ أَمَرْتُكَ⟫

What stopped you from disobedience when it was I who commanded you. Did Allah need to ask Iblees for his reasons? Does an owner. especially an owner like Allah.  need his property to give an explanation for why it is not behaving as it's supposed to? My pen stops writing. Am I going to ask it to present valid reasons for not writing anymore? No! I would just trash it and move on. So why is Allah asking Iblees for a reason. Because it is a gesture of disappointment. It is a gesture of an extremely loving Rabb being disappointed with his creation. You know I love you. You know who I am. You know my status. You know my knowledge encompasses all. You know I would NEVER EVER give an unjust command to obey. You know these things about me. I honored you by making you the leader and tutor of all angels. What possible reason could you have for disobeying me?

Scholars and linguists say. that this question that Allah asked Iblees. has a tone of humility just by itself. But what makes it EXTREMELY humble is when you look at the context of who is asking who. The creator. The Rabb is asking his creation. The king of kings is asking his slave. That makes this statement. extremely humble. But that also highlights the relationship of our creator with his creation. Allah being the ONLY one worthy of pride. deals with his creation with extreme humility.  SubhanAllah!

Now lets play devils advocate for a second. Is it possible that Iblees was ACTUALLY confused? Is it possible that maybe Iblees. in his ignorance made a mistake. because of his observation of the physical properties of fire and clay? Is that possible?

It's not. He actually knew exactly why Allah had asked him to bow down to Adam. He knew perfectly well that Adam AS was superior to him in knowledge. and there was absolutely no reason for him to disobey. How do we know that? Because of this ayah. where Allah talks about Iblees and says.

⟪ar-quote:وَإِذْ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ ٱسْجُدُوا۟ لِآدَمَ فَسَجَدُوٓا۟ إِلَّآ إِبْلِيسَ أَبَىٰ وَٱسْتَكْبَرَ وَكَانَ مِنَ ٱلْكَفِرِينَ⟫

And when I commanded the angles . prostrate to Adam. They all did except Iblis. He refused, became arrogant, and was thus amongst the Kaafireen. So the word Kafir is used for Iblis in this ayah. In another ayah Allah says.

⟪ar-quote:وَإِذْ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ ٱسْجُدُوا۟ لِآدَمَ فَسَجَدُوٓا۟ إِلَّآ إِبْلِيسَ كَانَ مِنَ ٱلْجِنِّ فَفَسَقَ عَنْ أَمْرِ رَبِّهِ⟫

And when I commanded the angles . prostrate to Adam. They all did except Iblis. He was one of the Jinns and he transgressed or broke the Command of his master. So in this ayah the word Fasaqa is used.

### Difference between KUFR and FISQ

So let's look at these two words.

Kafir comes from the word Kufr. which means to intentionally hide something. to hide a truth with intent. to deny a reality while realizing it. that's all Kufr. If you accidentally hide something. or you deny because you don't understand. thats not kufur.  that's Nisyaan.  Kufr is when one knows something and intentionally covers it up. You understand?

But Kaafir is the superlative form of the word which means someone who intentionally and constantly hides facts. It's not a one time thing. Kafir is someone who always. continuously. consistently covers things up.  That's why a farmer in Arabic is called a Kafir. because he has the seeds. and he hides them in the ground. He burries them in the ground. he covers it up with soil. and he does that for a living. So he does that over and over again.   So the one who covers up the truth.  constantly. consistently. intentionally is called a Kafir.

Faasiq comes from the word ⟪ar:فِسقْ⟫which means to break an agreement. To go out of bounds. But Faasiq. on the same phoenotic pattern as "Kaafir". means someone who ALWAYS goes out of bound. who intentionally and constantly transgresses.

So Iblees is Kafir AND Fasiq. He knew that Allah is his creator. He knew Allah is his Rabb. He understood that he was property and Allah was his owner. He knew the reality that Adam AS is superior to him. He still intentionally rejected his superiority. He knew his boundaries when it came to obeying Allah's commands. He knew his place in relation to the glorious position of Allah. Yet he INTENTONALLY transgressed.

He did both of these things. he rejected the truth. and he trangressed his boundaries. both through one single action. His disobedience.

So the problem was not that Iblees did not believe in Allah as his creator. An athiest does not believe in the existence of Allah. but Iblees did. His belief is clear in his own words.  He said:

⟪ar-quote:خَلَقْتَنِى مِن نَّارٍۢ وَخَلَقْتَهُۥ مِن طِينٍۢ⟫

You created me! he does not just believe in Allah.  he acknowledges Allah as his creator. He's talking to allah and he is accepting Allah as his creator. His kufr. Listen to this very carefully. His kufr. his disbelief.  is not in.  I don't believe Allah exists.  His disbelief is in his diobedience. I'll say that 3 times. 

**His disbelief is his disobedience X3**

Why am I saying it 3 times. Because you and I too believe in Allah as our creator. but we still disobey Him all the time.  and we say.  it's not that bad.  At least I still believe in allah. It's not like I'm a Kafir! I know I do some very messed up stuff.  I know.  but its not like I'm a disbeliever.

The disbelief of Iblees was his disobedience.

Iblees doesn't need to get you and me to disbelieve. All he needs to do.  is to get us to disobey. Thats all he needs. That's all he is trying to do. You and I REALLY need to understand this.   Because at the end of the day.  after disobeying allah. all we say is. Hey! at least I believe in allah. that should be good enough for me. then guess what? Iblees believed in Allah too. he did exactly that. that's why I repeated that 3 times. The disbelief of Iblees. The Kufr of Iblees.   was his disobedience.  Because through his disobedience he intentionally rejected and covered up the truth.

And through his disobedience he became Faasiq. He transgressed his boundaries.  and he broke the agreement with Allah. Have we made an agreement with Allah? . Something called Ahad Shareef. A promise we made with Allah. to pray 5 times a day. fast. give zakaat. do good. refrain from evil. Did we make that agreement with Allah?. Iblees broke his agreement with Allah through his disobedience. What are we doing?

And the root cause of it all was arrogance. Once our ego gives birth to arrogance. disobedience will just naturally and inevitably follow. And that's why both the Istiaaza (Falaq and Naas) begin with what? Qul! Declare! Delcare your submission. And as we learnt. our declaration of our need. removes arrogance from our hearts. It humbles the heart! Because that is what we learnt Shaytan attacks.  ⟪ar:الذی یوسوس فی صدور الناس⟫ . He attacks the chest of mankind. which contains what? . The heart! He instills arrogance and pride in our hearts through his whispers. 

So what got shaytan in trouble.  was not his disbelief in Allah. but his arrogance! His pride. What got him into trouble was his thinking. that he is better than Adam AS. What got him into trouble was his thinking. that he knows more than Allah. Cause Allah obviously doesn't know that fire is better than clay. right! Astaghfirullah!

His arrogance is what got him thrown out of jannah. But the greatest.  and sadly the MOST common sickness of our time. is Arrogance! And that's why you will notice all religious activities are designed around humility. They're are all exercises in humility. That's why when we pray.  what do we consntantly say? Allahu Akbar. Allahu Akbar.Allahu Akbar. Allah is greater!  Allah is greater! Allah is greater!.  Which means.  I am not! I am not! I am not! . And allah says when you disobey me. you are saying that YOU are greater! You think you are greater! that's disobedience!

---

Attributes of clay and fire

Now scholars have presented  another beautiful dimension of how flawed Iblees was in his logic of fire being superior than clay. So now let's look at the statement in a different light. Iblees said.
⟪ar-quote:خَلَقْتَنِى مِن نَّارٍۢ وَخَلَقْتَهُۥ مِن طِينٍۢ⟫

Let's first understand the meaning of the word Teen. Teen means damp mud. or damp dirt. It is commonly translated as clay. which is basically damp dirt. or damp soil if you will. In Urdu it would be translated to گیلی مٹی . or گارا .

Now there is another word in Arabic. Turaab. which means dry dirt. or dry mud. You add a bit of water to turaab and it becomes Teen. And BTW this word Turaab is also used in the Quran. On the day of judgment.
⟪ar-quote:وَيَقُولُ ٱلْكَافِرُ يَلَيْتَنِى كُنتُ تُرَبًۢا⟫

the kafir will say on the day of judgment. ٰٰI wish I was dry mud today. We'll look at this ayah in one of the future sessions InshaAllah!

So the first thing I want to understand is that Teen and Turaab are both the same thing. They're both dirt or soil.  Turaab is dry soil and Teen is damp soil. OK?  But we'll just call it clay. OK?

The argument Iblees made was based on a comparison of the external attributes of the substance they were made of. fire and clay. We talked about this earlier in some detail. He said fire is brighter. it is hotter. its flame rises. Clay on the other hand is dull. it is cold. and it falls to the ground. Therefore I am better than him! But what he intentionally chose to reject. what he intentionally chose to ignore and cover up. was that Allah did not ask the angels to prostrate before Adam until he blew his spirit into him. And soul is always greater than body. Spirituality is always superior to physicality. This is what we talked about the last time.

But now if we look at it. even from a physical stand point. Allah was completely JUST in asking fire.  to bow down before clay. Because even if the external attributes of fire may seem superior to that of clay. but the inner attributes.  and the inner qualities of clay.  are far superior to that of fire. The greatest reason is because clay is humble. It submits itself to the farmer who sows seeds within it. And because of its humility towards the farmer. soil allows for growth within it. It allows for new life to develop in its womb. It accepts and absorbs the water given by the farmer. and it uses that water to nurture the seeds.  into a fruit bearing tree. Fire on the other hand completely rejects water. There can be no growth. no development of life through fire.

That's the greatest and most important difference between clay and fire. It is the difference between humility and arrogance. The humility of clay or soil.  allows growth. it is nurturning. it is a source of life. It yields. it submits.

Fire on the other hand. only consumes.  and destroys and kills. It burns and destroys anything and everything that is placed within it. Try sowing a seed within fire. you're not going to get too far with it. But you sow those same seeds in soil. and it will give you back a tree loaded with fruits.

Clay. because of its humility.  can be moulded. it can be shaped into whatever form the creator desires. because it is humble. It submits itself to the hands of the potter. who shapes it in any way he feels is best. Clay is obedient. it does sajda.  because it submits itself to the will of the one its master allowing Him to shape it in whatever way He desires.  

Fire cannot be moulded. It cannot be shaped. Because it is disobedient.  it is arrogant. That's why clay is better than fire. We human beings. we were created from clay. which is supposed to be humble. Evil or sharr. which I told you comes from the word Sharara. a burning flame. its nature is arrogance.

Now is fire bright and luminous and attractive? Of course. that's why there is so much attraction in evil. That's why we are drawn towards evil. because of its bright dancing naked flames. it seduces us. it entices. mesmerizes us. it attracts us towards it. But once we get close. what does fire do? It engulfs us. burns us. destroys us. What happens to the most beautiful thing when it gets burnt? It becomes all black and charred and disfigured and distorted. That's what evil ends up doing to us. But in the beginning is it attractive? . Is it enticing? Absolutely! Partying all the time. drinking. smoking. watching filthy movies on the internet. Is there attraction in all of these things? Sure! Are their rewards immediate? . Do you get to have a good time right now? Sure!!. But where does it lead to? Where does that path end? Look at what alcohol evenutally lead to!. The person ends up being an alcoholic. He started drinking because it looked cool. But the same person. when engulfed and eaten and burnt by it. ends up becoming an alcoholic. What does the so COOL smoking eventually lead to? Cancer. Heart attack. Stroke.  Where does this shamelessness and internet filth lead to? Broken marriages. Where the only kind of relationship a man is capable of with his wife.  is what a moneky has with a female monkey. Honestly. examine any item that is prohibited in Islam. You will find two things in them. They will appear very attractive. and they will always end up in destruction. They all lead to one final destination. Destruction. Because that's what it is. FIRE!!! And fire as attractive and brilliant and beautiful it may seem. It burns. It incinerates. It always ends in pain and horror.

Now in comparison to that look at what soil does. Look at the job of a farmer. How attractive does farming or gardening seem? Not much. Seems pretty dull. pretty boring. tedious. doesn't it?.  The farmer keep investing time and effort. day after day. month after month.  and sees nothing. After months he see's something tiny sprout out of the dirt. It is extremely slow progress.  But when it comes time to harvest. what kind of yield does that soil produce? In tons! right? The fruits that are produced as a result of that slow. dull. hard labor. they have to be weighed in tons. And now what is the weight of those fruits.  in compairson to the weight of the seeds that were initially sown in the soil. No comparison. The reward that the farmer reaps at the end.  has no comparison to the intial trivial value of the seeds he sowed. Isn't that true?

Now do the rules of Islam seem dull? just like soil? Sure! Because Islam is exactly that. soil. And we are farmers planting the seeds of our belief in that soil. It's not the most attractive profession in the world. But when we sow the seeds of our belief and faith into it.and we water it with the knowledge given to us by our elders. our daat. And we farm them. cultivate them.  by striving day in and day out with our taharah, namaaz, fasts, zakaat, hajj.   What does that very dull soil give us back? Beautiful. lush. fruit bearing trees. Rewards that cannot even be compared to the initial investment.  But is it a long tedious. repetitive process? Sure! But look at the quantity and the quality of reward at the end.

The exterior of fire is beautiful. but its interior is destruction and death. The exterior of EVIL is beautiful. it is attractive. it is enticing. it is mesmerizing. But it will always result in pain and suffering and destruction in this life and the after life.

The exterior of clay is dull. but its interior is growth and life. The exterior of Islam. the exterior of Shariah may seem dull. it may seem inconvenient. demanding. but once we submit to it. willingly. in obedience. it's end result is immense growth. its end result is life. ultimate success in this life and the after life.

Fire brings death and destruction. Clay produces eternal life.

And that is what Iblees chose. He chose the external attraction. He preferred the external and immediate brilliance of fire.  to the internal essence of clay. And this is the lesson we have to learn from this story. We have to learn from this terrible mistake of Iblees. He chose the external form. over the internal essence. This duniya is fire. Listen to this very carefully. This duniya. this world we live in. it is FIRE.  for the one who wants immediate rewards. If you want to. what people call. ENJOY your life. Go right ahead! You'll get your immediate rewards. no doubt about it. And it'll feel amazingly good too. So if you are craving to commit those forbidden things. then go ahead. But just know. that it will end up in death and destruction in this life and the after life. Because this duniya is fire for the one who wants immediate rewards.

And this same duniya is clay for the one who is willing to defer his enjoyment. his pleasures for a incomparibly greater reward. This duniya is both fire and clay. It is now up to you and I. what we choose for ourselves. Iblees preferred fire and we know where that led him to. Adam chose clay and we also know where that led him to. Both paths are open for us.

And that's why using the Istiaaza. we declare our humility to Allah by seeking and entering his protection. from what? From the fire of Sharr. from the attractions of evil. because we realize. that even though shaytan's path is attractive. its brilliant. its bright. its mesmerizing. It ONLY ends up in destruction and terrible pain. the pain of heat. the pain of burning.  But once we submit to the protection of Islam. we restrain ourselves within the confines of Shariah. We sow our selves. willingly and in obedience. into the soil of Rabb AlFalaq. Rabb AlNaas. Malik AlNaas. Ilah AlNaas. the end result is magnificent. it is growth. it is beauty. The end result is delicious life giving fruits in the hereafter.
